  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_65fa6e61-e9ed-4a87-ba81-bbaceaf980ec'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    };

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/39746437-jon"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/39746437-jon">Jon</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Book 1 is merely the start of what ends up being quite an epic tale. The books mature from being cheesy to being very serious later on. This book is a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Book 1 is merely the start of what ends up being quite an epic tale. The books mature from being cheesy to being very serious later on. This book is also party of a several book story arc. Not much thrilling really happens in this book. It's more about being a teenager, and her awakening to herself. The books after this take on a darker tone. The characters also mature into adults. The series covers decades and a vast plot reaching centuries past and present.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_144447527" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144447527" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144447527?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-witches">pn-witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=ruined-series">ruined-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144447527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16918455246746009744">This review is really about the whole Sweep series, but I'm putting it with Book One because that's where people will go to find out whether all of them are worth reading. I started out really enjoying the series, then HATED WITH A PASSION what seemed to be going on, and then am left now feeling really sad and cheated. I've never started out liking a series and then turned around and felt so angry and disappointed and sad after it ended. <br/><br/>Firstly, I have to say that I really enjoyed books 1 - 6. </span>
  <span id="freeText16918455246746009744" style="display:none">This review is really about the whole Sweep series, but I'm putting it with Book One because that's where people will go to find out whether all of them are worth reading. I started out really enjoying the series, then HATED WITH A PASSION what seemed to be going on, and then am left now feeling really sad and cheated. I've never started out liking a series and then turned around and felt so angry and disappointed and sad after it ended. <br /><br />Firstly, I have to say that I really enjoyed books 1 - 6. Some are stronger than others, but overall they are well-written and packed with action, plus the whole wicca thing is well-researched and really interesting to read about. Morgan is also an interesting character who goes through a lot of personal growth and development, and her attraction to the new boy in town and her feelings about her friend Bree and her parents and her sister (et al) are completely relatable. I also liked books 8, 9, and 12, and would give these nine books 3.5-4 out of 5 stars. <br /><br />Spoiler-free things I never cared for, right from the very beginning: <br /><br />* the books are too short. They're literally half the size of a typical YA novel (way to drag out a series) and nearly every one ended on an abrupt cliffhanger. I kept clicking forward on my Kindle, thinking there was something glitchy going on with my e-reader, but it turns out the writing just...stopped. Annoying and unnecessary, since there is a way to both give closure to a volume and whet an appetite for the next novel without making your readers feel as if you've yanked the covers off them. <br /><br />* the stories that did not relate directly to Morgan's narrative diluted the books. Some detail is enjoyable, but when so few characters really have anything to do at all (back to this later) and there is so much time spent re-hashing everyone's mundane dating details in every single book when it doesn't affect anything else, it gets really boring really fast. As such, I never really cared for the bit at the beginning of each chapter that was an "excerpt" from a journal entry or book on magick. The only time I felt it really added to the book were when you got a glimpse of what Hunter was feeling in towards the earlier part of the series. And yes, this means Alisa too--one of the least interesting secondary characters who shows up late and then suddenly got POV narrative and her own book. The more the series went on, the more time was spent with other characters, and the series was less strong as a result.<br /><br />I did think narrating a book from Hunter's point of view was interesting, until his story went way far away from Morgan's. This might've been okay if the book had been longer and their relationship more fleshed out after he returns AND....<br /><br />**SPOILER ALERT for the rest of this review*<br /><br />* ....if he didn't freaking cheat on her while he's gone. (for just two weeks! in Canada!) This was such a slap in the face after everything that happened with Cal and drawing out their will they-won't they relationship for more than 10 books. I don't understand why this was put in at all, because there is nearly no time devoted to resolving how Morgan would really feel about this happening afterwards. There are literally maybe 5 short paragraphs contained over two books to deal with this, which is completely unrealistic for any girl, no matter what else was going on. And for someone like Morgan, who was already betrayed by his brother? Completely impossible that she would have gotten over it so quickly.<br /><br />* By the time I finished Book 13, I was so ready for Morgan and Hunter to get things resolved already. Since I was already pretty much skimming through anything that wasn't Morgan or Hunter's narrative, I skipped Book 14 entirely and then I read about the HUGE thing that happens in the beginning of Book 15. After reading the sample chapter (read it, read it, it's linked on Amazon), I couldn't believe an author would invest so much of her readers' time and emotion only to kill off a main character like that for no apparent reason. I felt so angry and so cheated, and I swore I would never read anything by this author again. It was only after I read the spoiler-y reviews on Good Reads that I decided to read the rest of the book--and even after things were resolved, I still have very mixed emotions about the whole thing. <br /><br />You barely spend any time with Morgan and Hunter in the beginning before things end (literally, maybe 15 pages in) and the whole thing just goes off-kilter from there. Morgan doesn't learn anything from Hunter's death and we have no time at all to mourn him ourselves until all the sudden she's married, had a child, and had her husband die on her. Everyone whose lives you heard so much about in the series is also pretty much dumped here, with just a couple mentions of what happened to Bree and Mary K. This is because they don't matter in the big scheme of things, and apparently they never did.<br /><br />Like many of the other readers here, I was fine with Moira but I really could have done without her and mostly just skimmed the book impatiently until Hunter shows up again. And while I'm happy they got a happy ending, I still feel drained and sad and upset over the whole thing. Poor Hunter is hugely diminished in this book, and you never really get a sense of how awful his island imprisonment was. You also don't get much emotional satisfaction once he comes back--so little time is spent on his homecoming and recovery, and as another reader pointed out, is he really going to stay in the guest bedroom once he (soul mate and father) comes home? There is no anguish, no comforting, no healing, no real emotional truth or connection. It all just felt completely unrealistic and sad. <br /><br />I've never been so disappointed in a series that I liked. Because of the way everything was dragged on and on (these would have been better condensed into maybe 5 - 6 books, with a lot of things edited out) and because of the huge emotional battering that did NOT make me feel fulfilled and happy at the end, I would not recommend this series to anyone. I started out giving this series a 3 out of 5 stars, but as I wrote this review I realized a more accurate rating would be a 2. Because no matter how much I enjoyed some of the books, the others were not worth the time and money and emotional investment. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16918455246746009744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9768654502703034056"><b>3 stars - It was good.</b><br/><br/>The writing is only so-so, average at best with shallow cardboard characters. It does seem to be well researched and it is interesting to see many of the myths about Wicca confronted. <br/>-------------------------------------------<br/><b>First Sentence:</b> Years from now I’ll look back and remember today as the day I met him.<br/></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10110698328152608817">I'm so late to this series but very excited to continue on with the next books!<br/><br/>3.5 out of 5 stars<br/><br/>Book of Shadows follows a young girl called Morgan, who lives in a strong Catholic family and attends church every Sunday. Morgan and her school friends start becoming interested in all of the beliefs surrounding Wicca but has to keep this a secret from her family. She then discovers something about herself </span>
  <span id="freeText10110698328152608817" style="display:none">I'm so late to this series but very excited to continue on with the next books!<br /><br />3.5 out of 5 stars<br /><br />Book of Shadows follows a young girl called Morgan, who lives in a strong Catholic family and attends church every Sunday. Her school life changes with the arrival of a new boy called Cal, who is a practising Wiccan. Morgan and her school friends start becoming interested in all of the beliefs surrounding Wicca but has to keep this a secret from her family. She then discovers something about herself that she never even knew, she is part of the witches! It was interesting as the reader learning more about Catholicism (I did go to a Catholic High School) and Wicca. What let the story down for me a little was a dislike towards Morgan's friend Bree as a character. Halfway through, she acts quite snarky and bitchy towards Morgan but this change does tie back to Cal's character. The pacing was quite fast and story length short however, did get to the point. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10110698328152608817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3063657657" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3063657657" />
    <a title="Amber J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66639925-amber-j"><img alt="Amber J" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579805098p2/66639925.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3063657657?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber J" href="/user/show/66639925-amber-j">Amber J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66639925-amber-j?shelf=2019-reading-challenge">2019-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66639925-amber-j?shelf=5-stars-of-2019">5-stars-of-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3063657657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer146275554832885736"><b>
  <i>“I saw something last night-a flash of power from an unexpected source. I can't jump to conclusions - I've been looking and waiting and watching for too long to make a mistake. But in my gut I feel she's here. She's here and she has power. I need to get closer to her.”<br/>― Cate Tiernan, Book of Shadows</i>
</b><br/><br/><i>I try to express only my most honest opinion in a spoiler free way. If you feel anything in my review is a spoiler and is not already hidden in spoiler brackets please let me know. Thank you.</i><br/><p>Morga</p></span>
  <span id="freeText146275554832885736" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“I saw something last night-a flash of power from an unexpected source. I can't jump to conclusions - I've been looking and waiting and watching for too long to make a mistake. But in my gut I feel she's here. She's here and she has power. I need to get closer to her.”<br />― Cate Tiernan, Book of Shadows</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>I try to express only my most honest opinion in a spoiler free way. If you feel anything in my review is a spoiler and is not already hidden in spoiler brackets please let me know. Thank you.</i><br /><p>Morgan is a typical teenage girl. Her best friend is Bree, who is popular and pretty. When she meets Cal, he introduces Morgan, Bree, and others of there group to wicca. Soon Morgan realizes that might be more to it then just a different religion. She realizes she wants to be a witch. And she finds herself drawn to Cal and possible him to her as well.</p><br /><p>First off I want to say sorry for my crappy blurb. I read this book a few weeks ago already and just now getting around to reviewing it. I really loved this book. I was actually a bit surprised how much considering how short it is, but the characters where well written and had distinct personalities. Morgan's so called best friend Bree is just a horrible friend though, and I hope that as the series continues Morgan realizes this and stays away from the overly toxic relationship. It follows a similar YA pattern. There is a bit of a love triangle and of course everyone is apparently SOOO attractive and then the main character being SPECIAL in some way. This is normal for its genre and I don't hold it against it. I will definitely be finishing this series. I can't wait to see how the story and characters develop from here on out.</p><br /><p>
  <i>How I choose my rating:<br />1* Did not finish, or hated it but forced myself to finish.<br />2** Didn't really like it. Didn't hate it but not sure why I finished it other then for some closure.<br />3*** I liked it. I had some issues with it, but as a whole it was good. I probably won't reread again ever, but there is a chance I might finish the series. (If part of one) But if not it's not a huge loss.<br />4**** I really liked this book. Maybe not a work of genius, but highly entertaining. I might reread this again, and I will finish the series. (If part of one) I would recommend to those I know hold interest in this books content.<br />5***** I loved this book. I found little to no issues with it at all. I will definitely be rereading this and probably more than once. I will finish the series and reread it multiple times. (If part of one) I will recommend this book to EVERYONE!!!!</i>
</p></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer940128532880556720">Reviewed by Michaela Pallante aka "Mickey" for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>Morgan Rowlands is a normal teenage girl. She gets good grades, hangs out with her friends, and goes to church with her family on Sundays. Nothing out of the ordinary ever happens to her... until she meets Cal Blaire. <br/><br/>Cal is the new cute senior who has just transferred to Widow's Vale High.   <span id="freeText940128532880556720" style="display:none">Reviewed by Michaela Pallante aka "Mickey" for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Morgan Rowlands is a normal teenage girl. She gets good grades, hangs out with her friends, and goes to church with her family on Sundays. Nothing out of the ordinary ever happens to her... until she meets Cal Blaire. <br /><br />Cal is the new cute senior who has just transferred to Widow's Vale High. His looks aren't the only thing that sets him apart from other boys. He's Wiccan, a different religion than Morgan and one that she has never come into contact with before. <br /><br />Something about Cal and his religion interests Morgan and her best friends, Bree and Robbie. The more they hang out with Cal, the more they like him. While with Cal, Morgan learns something about herself that completely blows her mind -- and may change her life forever. <br /><br />This book was fun to read. The story was great and you learn a thing or two about Wicca as you read it (it's not scary!). BOOK OF SHADOWS is the first of 14 books, plus a super edition novel, so this is only the start of Morgan and Cal's adventures. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8775428336750173218">Wow! What can I say without completely ruining this book?<br/><br/>In previous reviews; I have complained about books with way too much page filler but not this book! It is a small, quick, easy and entertaining read!<br/><br/>Unlike a lot of the other Urban Fantasy books I have been reading lately, this book seemed really lifelike! I could see how this would make someone curious about Wicca. I don't believe in "Wicca" or White Magic but I could see how this book could make someone really want to study into it.<br/><br/>Morga</span>
  <span id="freeText8775428336750173218" style="display:none">Wow! What can I say without completely ruining this book?<br /><br />In previous reviews; I have complained about books with way too much page filler but not this book! It is a small, quick, easy and entertaining read!<br /><br />Unlike a lot of the other Urban Fantasy books I have been reading lately, this book seemed really lifelike! I could see how this would make someone curious about Wicca. I don't believe in "Wicca" or White Magic but I could see how this book could make someone really want to study into it.<br /><br />Morgan is just an average shy girl with a very popular best friend Bree! Morgan and Bree have been best friends since they were young kids. Even with Morgan and Bree hanging out in two completely different crowds, it never dampens their close relationship.<br /><br />There is a new boy in their school. Cal Blaire. The moment he walks up to the school, everyone's head turns in his direction. All the girls immediately salivate over his olive skin and gold colored eyes. To make it even worse, Morgan isn’t immune to the crazy obsession! Morgan has never been fully in to a guy before now; she has never had a boyfriend or even her first kiss. She is automatically drawn to Cal but she knows that he is way out of her league.<br /><br />Once everyone starts getting to know Cal; just about everyone either wants to be his friend or just “wants him period”. The exception is all the guys that are jealous that their girlfriend gawk at Cal right in front of them. Cal doesn’t fall into a click to “hang” with, he just accepts each person the same as the next. Morgan admires this about Cal; he even goes out of his way to start multiple conversations with her! Her one concern is that she thinks he is a player. He goes on dates with girls but just goes from one to the next.<br /><br />One day, Cal goes around the school to all the Junior and Senior students to invite them to a party. The directions he gives them leads the partygoers to a large field and this is when Cal introduces Wicca. This meeting wakes up something in Morgan.<br /><br />I am going to immediately start the second book to the series and I this is a book that I would highly recommend!<br /><br /><b>Follow my blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://MagicalUrbanFantasyReads.com/">http://MagicalUrbanFantasyReads.com/</a> </b><br /><br /></span>

    <a title="Scribblegirl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1039260-scribblegirl"><img alt="Scribblegirl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454155364p2/1039260.jpg" /></a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1039260-scribblegirl?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1039260-scribblegirl?shelf=teen-reads">teen-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1039260-scribblegirl?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1039260-scribblegirl?shelf=mean-teens">mean-teens</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44933501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer245586867705949809">Scale of 1-10: 4<br/>Pros: Tiernan's writing does not suck, and she might be able to get decent mileage out of her story, as the books are short and quick reads.<br/>Cons: Struck me as a Harry Potter retread with an older, female heroine.<br/><br/>Synopsis: Morgan Rowlands finds out she's got a talent for witchcraft after superhot, supernatural Cal Blaire moves to her small, upstate NY town and starts slingin' the magic mojo around...not that anyone seems to notice or think it's weird. <br/><br/>My take: In a nutshell? Tiern</span>
  <span id="freeText245586867705949809" style="display:none">Scale of 1-10: 4<br />Pros: Tiernan's writing does not suck, and she might be able to get decent mileage out of her story, as the books are short and quick reads.<br />Cons: Struck me as a Harry Potter retread with an older, female heroine.<br /><br />Synopsis: Morgan Rowlands finds out she's got a talent for witchcraft after superhot, supernatural Cal Blaire moves to her small, upstate NY town and starts slingin' the magic mojo around...not that anyone seems to notice or think it's weird. <br /><br />My take: In a nutshell? Tiernan is lazy. She tells us how her characters feel, rather than describing their reactions and letting us see it; shrugs details off as supernatural magic mojo instead of giving any real reason for events to occur; and tends to bludgeon her readers with the Big Bat of Foreshadowing instead of dropping a subtle trail of bread crumbs leading up to the big revelation(s). Basically, the story goes a gorgeous new guy moves to town and all the girls are drawn to him. Magick, jealousy, and chick fights ensue...sort of like an episode of Dark Shadows - if Barnabus Collins were a magic-slinging high school senior. Or maybe more like The Wiccan Bachelor meets My So-Called Life...</span>
  <a data-text-id="245586867705949809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1921882470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1921882470" />
    <a title="Thomas Clairmont" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50173206-thomas-clairmont"><img alt="Thomas Clairmont" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580071772p2/50173206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1921882470?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Clairmont" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Clairmont" href="/user/show/50173206-thomas-clairmont">Thomas Clairmont</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1921882470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5466712833410256442">I finally found my "guilty pleasure" book series!<br/>It was very entertaining and I loved the story so much!<br/>At first, it was really difficult for me to memorize all of the characters but once you read the first 10 chapters, this feeling is gone!<br/>I am glad to see that this book series has a huge number of books because I am so curious where it will go! <br/>I DIDN'T EXPECTED THIS ENDING AND I AM STILL IN A STATE OF SHOCK BUT SO HAPPY AT THE SAME TIME!<br/>Oh and I really want to learn more about Cal in the next</span>
  <span id="freeText5466712833410256442" style="display:none">I finally found my "guilty pleasure" book series!<br />It was very entertaining and I loved the story so much!<br />At first, it was really difficult for me to memorize all of the characters but once you read the first 10 chapters, this feeling is gone!<br />I am glad to see that this book series has a huge number of books because I am so curious where it will go! <br />I DIDN'T EXPECTED THIS ENDING AND I AM STILL IN A STATE OF SHOCK BUT SO HAPPY AT THE SAME TIME!<br />Oh and I really want to learn more about Cal in the next books, and I am sure will!<br /><br />If you still haven't read this series, I would say that it is never too late! This first book was a really fast read, very entertaining, I learnt a lot about Wicca and I think that it was extremely interesting! I'll for sure do some researches on this topic!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5466712833410256442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4822087824801969651" style="display:none">This was a fun story about witches, magic, and wicca! I loved Morgan and how she was fascinated by wicca. I wasn't so much of a fan about the focus on Cal and how attractive he was. I think it didn't really bring the story anything.         <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1680967703" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10875305877533353788">Read in 2017<br/>Read in 2014<br/>Read in 2009<br/>Read in 2003<br/><br/>2017- This marks my 4th time reading this book. For the new reader I must emphasize that these books mature as you read. They start off seeming like cheesy teenage fiction on a cringe worthy level, but they evolve into a truly grand, wonderful and epic story of the coming of age, and the realization of remarkable heritage.<br/><br/>A plain unassuming wallflower finds she is anything but ordinary. In fact, she is extraordinary! As she follows a path seeming d</span>
  <span id="freeText10875305877533353788" style="display:none">Read in 2017<br />Read in 2014<br />Read in 2009<br />Read in 2003<br /><br />2017- This marks my 4th time reading this book. For the new reader I must emphasize that these books mature as you read. They start off seeming like cheesy teenage fiction on a cringe worthy level, but they evolve into a truly grand, wonderful and epic story of the coming of age, and the realization of remarkable heritage.<br /><br />A plain unassuming wallflower finds she is anything but ordinary. In fact, she is extraordinary! As she follows a path seeming destined, her heart follows that of one she thinks beyond its reach. Lying within this likewise unassuming YA novel is a true gem, wrought with heartache and heartbreak. Will a straining friendship collapse amid the pressure of it all, leaving a bitterness in its wake. For Morgan Rowlands, she must suffer trials of family and friend alike to reach a crossroads long destined for and to choose a path which seems contrary to her upbringing.<br /><br />Ignore the awful reviews. This series is a gem among the vast heaps of horrid YA novels out there. Once you've devoured book one, and begun the second, there'll be no stopping you!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10875305877533353788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer307309415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer543178418974944113"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404251280i/10214586.png' width='400' height='171' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This review was originally published on <a href='http://beckysblogs.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blogs of a Bookaholic</a>.<br/><br/><b>A fantastic first book full of magic, mystery and discovery.</b> <br/>This is around the 4/5 time I've read this book now and it never disappoints! I first discovered this series aged 14, and in a weird way, I almost feel like the books chose me. They came to me in a point in my life where I really needed them, and held for me some key advice and life lessons that helped me deal with several big changes going on at that time. These books are i</span>
  <span id="freeText543178418974944113" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404251280i/10214586.png" width="400" height="171" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review was originally published on <a href="http://beckysblogs.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blogs of a Bookaholic</a>.<br><br><b>A fantastic first book full of magic, mystery and discovery.</b> <br>This is around the 4/5 time I've read this book now and it never disappoints! I first discovered this series aged 14, and in a weird way, I almost feel like the books chose me. They came to me in a point in my life where I really needed them, and held for me some key advice and life lessons that helped me deal with several big changes going on at that time. These books are incredibly underrated and in my opinion deserve a much bigger spotlight.<br><br>Now, the writing in this book is not what you would consider ‘good’ technical writing. Character descriptions aren't integrated in a subtle way, they are laid out pure and simple from the first moment we meet each character. There are a few instances of awkward phrasing, and there are no super fancy words. But the beauty of <i>Tiernan’s</i> writing lies in its simplicity. For every standard description there is also a unique or interesting passage from a narrative voice that is yet to reach its peak. It always amazes me how <i>Tiernan</i> packs so much into such a small amount of pages, and there is not one dull moment. <br><br>The plot is consistently fast paced and there is no unneeded meandering or boring chapters. It brings together a lot of typical YA story-lines, two best friends in an unequal relationship feuding over the same guy, teenage insecurities and family fights, yet I feel like it is dealt with in a much less superficial way. It’s realistic and believable. What I also love about this book is that although romance and lusting after a guy is a key plot point, (and is pretty over-dramatic) it is not the main focus. Instead it centers more on Morgan’s involvement with the religion Wicca, and through it her own self discovery. I would be lying if I didn't say the biggest reason I love these books is my genuine fascination with the religion. <br><br><i>Tiernan</i> also has a knack for creating great vivid characters; simple little things such as Morgan's addiction to Diet Coke make her feel all the more realistic. She’s got spunk, but not in a typically cliched over the top YA way, and her integrity and the way she sticks to her convictions make her stand out from the crowd.<br>Bree, who at first seems like the stereotypical sassy boy obsessed best friend found in so many YA books, is quickly given much more depth and complexity. Robbie is sweet and loyal, Cal is mysterious and yet instantly likable. They are all interesting, and remarkably fleshed out for such a small book.<br><br>One of my all time favourite series, and I would recommend it to everyone! xD<br><br><b>You can check out my full, unabridged review and others like it <a href="http://beckysblogs.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blogs of a Bookaholic</a>. :)</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="543178418974944113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_128502429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128502429" />
    <a title="Shalor T." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4436152-shalor-t"><img alt="Shalor T." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288335161p2/4436152.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128502429?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shalor T." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shalor T." href="/user/show/4436152-shalor-t">Shalor T.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128502429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18434621485068255893">First off, let me say that if you are looking for a true to life portrayal of the Wiccan faith, look elsewhere. Yes, the author has taken great pains to stay as close to the actual practice as possible, but she still takes several liberties in order to make for a good story. Even so, this is one of the very few mainstream series I've read that actually gets the main gist of the Pagan religion. <br/><br/>Now for the story. The story focuses around Morgan, a somewhat normal girl. When the cute new boy in sc</span>
  <span id="freeText18434621485068255893" style="display:none">First off, let me say that if you are looking for a true to life portrayal of the Wiccan faith, look elsewhere. Yes, the author has taken great pains to stay as close to the actual practice as possible, but she still takes several liberties in order to make for a good story. Even so, this is one of the very few mainstream series I've read that actually gets the main gist of the Pagan religion. <br /><br />Now for the story. The story focuses around Morgan, a somewhat normal girl. When the cute new boy in school asks her to come to a field for a secret party, she jumps at the chance to do so. (As does her best friend.) Once there she discovers that the new boy Cal wants them all to help perform magic, and despite some initial misgivings Morgan does. What follows after is a discovery about her true potential as a witch as well as her taking the first step in a path that will eventually put everyone she loves in danger. <br /><br />Like I said initially, there's a lot of liberty taken with the whole Wiccan religion. They bring in the idea of "Blood Witches" that come from a specific bloodline as well as add in magic that isn't possible. Don't take offense at this- maybe it's overly done but it's still more realistic than half of the other series out there right now &amp; the author does do the research. <br /><br />The best way to describe this series is to compare it to a piece of chocolate. It's way yummy &amp; fun, and when each book is about 160 pages the books don't seem to last very long. It's very much worth reading &amp; I recommend this series to anyone with a hunger for fantasy reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18434621485068255893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45913578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45913578" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45913578?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of The Secret Circle series</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=witches">witches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45913578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5942825308294389721">I enjoyed this book; it was a nice quick read. It reminded me a lot of the series <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3099780.The_Secret_Circle_No__1_The_Initiation_and_The_Captive_Part_I' title='The Secret Circle No. 1 The Initiation and The Captive Part I by L.J. Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret Circle No. 1 The Initiation and The Captive Part I</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/50873.L_J__Smith' title='L.J. Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>L.J. Smith</a>. I read those when I was a teen and I think if I had found Tiernan's series then I would have eaten them up as well.<br/><br/>This book sets up the series and it ends at a place where you absolutely <i>need</i> to pick up the next one to see what happens.<br/><br/>I don't read a whole lot of books on witches anymore, I think I grew out of them a bit when I graduated </span>
  <span id="freeText5942825308294389721" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book; it was a nice quick read. It reminded me a lot of the series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3099780.The_Secret_Circle_No__1_The_Initiation_and_The_Captive_Part_I" title="The Secret Circle No. 1 The Initiation and The Captive Part I by L.J. Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret Circle No. 1 The Initiation and The Captive Part I</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/50873.L_J__Smith" title="L.J. Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">L.J. Smith</a>. I read those when I was a teen and I think if I had found Tiernan's series then I would have eaten them up as well.<br /><br />This book sets up the series and it ends at a place where you absolutely <i>need</i> to pick up the next one to see what happens.<br /><br />I don't read a whole lot of books on witches anymore, I think I grew out of them a bit when I graduated high school, although this book was sort of nostalgic for me. I remember going to occult bookstores when I knew my parents, well, at least my Dad, would be upset if they knew that's where I'd been. I think just about every girl goes through their phase that includes Ouija boards, "seances", and playing light as a feather - stiff as a board. I liked reading Book of Shadows because it made me remember all those silly times with my friends. Although we never went skinny dipping in the moonlight ... <br /><br />I enjoyed this book a lot and I'm definitely going to have to start the next one soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5942825308294389721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_246390046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246390046" />
    <a title="Kaisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3017954-kaisa"><img alt="Kaisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546447572p2/3017954.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246390046?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaisa" href="/user/show/3017954-kaisa">Kaisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246390046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9150189920857335822">Nononononono T_T I wanted this book to be good. But then again, what was I thinking? If a book is 160 pages long.. and also a part of a series with three gazillion other books... it just can't be good.<br/><br/>I don't know why, but recently I've been interested in wicca. It's probably cuz I've been re-watching Charmed. The TV show.<br/>Anyway, that's why I bought the first three books in this series. I wanted to read about witches. <br/><br/>This book is about a bunch of teens who get involved with a wiccan witch dude </span>
  <span id="freeText9150189920857335822" style="display:none">Nononononono T_T I wanted this book to be good. But then again, what was I thinking? If a book is 160 pages long.. and also a part of a series with three gazillion other books... it just can't be good.<br /><br />I don't know why, but recently I've been interested in wicca. It's probably cuz I've been re-watching Charmed. The TV show.<br />Anyway, that's why I bought the first three books in this series. I wanted to read about witches. <br /><br />This book is about a bunch of teens who get involved with a wiccan witch dude who just moved into town. He wants to start up a new coven, and they think he's all fascinating and stuff. The main character is a girl who is especially affected by the wiccan magick (is that how it's spelled in wicca? I think so) and.... of course, she's also infatuated with the wiccan boy.<br />That's pretty much it!! Not much can happen in 160 pages. <br />Seriously, what's the point in splitting the books up this way? It's like 'Vampire Kisses'. Totally weird.<br /><br />Oh, and the best friend is way too much of a bitch. There's no way they were friends before this. Who'd want to be friends with that? No way. I'm not buying it.<br /><br />This book is not well written. It's too short. There's nothing to it. I'm sorry =(</span>
  <a data-text-id="9150189920857335822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_8297323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8297323" />
    <a title="Loren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/581175-loren"><img alt="Loren" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8297323?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Loren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Loren" href="/user/show/581175-loren">Loren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">teenagers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8297323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5420959444112173111">A wonderful start to 'Sweep'/'Wicca'. *Spoilers books 1-4*<br/><br/>Tiernan has an incredible talent for creating uniquely vivid characters. Normally I shy away from books written in the 1st person, but this was pleasantly different. <br/><br/>The vulnerable nature of the main character means we can begin to empathise with her unusually quickly. This also blinds us to simple truths such as Hunter and Sky's true natures. We stand united with Morgan against them and we too feel crushed at Cal's betrayal. <br/><br/>The ending i</span>
  <span id="freeText5420959444112173111" style="display:none">A wonderful start to 'Sweep'/'Wicca'. *Spoilers books 1-4*<br /><br />Tiernan has an incredible talent for creating uniquely vivid characters. Normally I shy away from books written in the 1st person, but this was pleasantly different. <br /><br />The vulnerable nature of the main character means we can begin to empathise with her unusually quickly. This also blinds us to simple truths such as Hunter and Sky's true natures. We stand united with Morgan against them and we too feel crushed at Cal's betrayal. <br /><br />The ending is a little forced. The electricity was obviously there between them. Cate didn't need to end it on that note, we would have read the next one anyway.<br /><br />This book introduces many running themes of the series; Cal, Morgan's lineage, Christianity vs Wicca. Some people might view this one as a little slow moving... but the rest of the series makes up for that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5420959444112173111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9k3vp6BW5Sg98Da2Fw7qxuTV8UjVTaKiExfddwIUelsDOC8ITqeNoSkZI+1Klxrk6kfB+FbVS0GLThSKHLdbLQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vrAoMEzlQxnbkxyG7jMSSFQUvxhOaKn9h/lrZNHbbSBLxeifohQrkM96Cd2zquJqWoaPqM3wQB4foKKZz3hMVg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/191456.Cate_Tiernan">About Cate Tiernan</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/191456.Cate_Tiernan"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1224300007p3/191456.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/191456.Cate_Tiernan">Cate Tiernan
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,490
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11806938057534785029">"was born in New Orleans, LA, in 1961. New Orleans is one of the most interesting American cities, and it has an incredibly rich and exotic culture that had a profound influence on me. Kids in other cities have lemonade stands; we sold voodoo gris-gris and made wax dolls in the likenesses of our enemies. It's a very beautiful city, and the constant heat and humidity make gardens grow out of contro</span>
  <span id="freeText11806938057534785029" style="display:none">"was born in New Orleans, LA, in 1961. New Orleans is one of the most interesting American cities, and it has an incredibly rich and exotic culture that had a profound influence on me. Kids in other cities have lemonade stands; we sold voodoo gris-gris and made wax dolls in the likenesses of our enemies. It's a very beautiful city, and the constant heat and humidity make gardens grow out of control. There's an air of lassitude there, a general acceptance of eccentic or flamboyant behavior--the heat simply makes people do crazy things.<br /><br />I went to school in New York, and after school went back to New Orleans. Then I went back to New York (Manhattan) and got a job in publishing and started writing. My first book, a young, middle-grade chapter book, was published in 1990.<br /><br />Living in Manhattan was incredible, even though I didn't have a lot of money. There was so much to do and see, and so many interesting people to watch. There was a lot of frenetic energy there, and sometimes that felt very wearing and hard to live with. After eight years I was ready for a change, and my husband and I moved back to New Orleans. (Are you seeing a pattern here?)<br /><br />(While I was in NY, I helped edit "The Secret Circle" by L.J. Smith. I thought it was great.)<br /><br />We stayed in New Orleans five years. By the time we had two small children we knew we had to find someplace safer to live. I was glad my children were born in New Orleans--I had been born there, and my father had, and his father had, and his father had and so on. There was something about the connection of generations of blood coming from one place that I found very primal and important.<br /><br />Now I live in a cohousing community in Durham, NC. This is the most suburban place I've ever lived, and it's very different from living right in the middle of a city. For one thing, there aren't enough coffee shops. However, it's incredibly safe, and the community is very important to me. There are a lot of strong women here, and I find them inspiring.<br /><br />Am I a witch? Well, no. Even Wicca is too organized a religion for me. I'm much more idiosyncratic and just need to do my own thing, which is kind of new-agey and pantheistic. It's not that I don't work or play well with others, but I need to decide for myself when I do a certain thing, and how I do it. However, I can really relate to Wicca, and I so appreciate its woman-centeredness and its essentially female identity. I love those aspects, among others.<br /><br />I have several favorite writers. Barbara Hambly has been the biggest influence on how I describe magic. She's an incredibly imaginative and empathetic writer with a gift for creating a rich, sensual world. I love Barbara Pym, an English writer whose books came out mostly in the fifties. She was a master at describing the thousand tiny moments that make up a woman's day; how the seemingly small and inconsequential thing can suddenly take on a huge emotional importance. I greatly admire P.D. James. She's one of the very few writers who makes me actually look up words in the dictionary. She has a beautiful, precise, educated command of the language that leaves me in awe. I love Philip Larkin's poetry. I read a lot of nonfiction and also have some favorite romance writers. Before anyone groans, let me say that these women write really well about women trying to achieve emotional fulfillment, and that's kind of what we're all doing, right? I also just like reading about sex. Anyway, Jennifer Crusie, Susan Elizabeth Phillips, and early Linda Howard are my faves.<br /><br />And then of course there's my dark side, but more on that later.<br /><br />" -<a href="http://firefairy.eve7k.com/author/about_cate.php" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a><br /><br />Cate Tiernan is a pseudonym for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13613.Gabrielle_Charbonnet" rel="nofollow noopener">Gabrielle Charbonnet</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11806938057534785029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
